Local News of This Port

Sino-Japanese Tariff Negotiations Hold Formal Meeting Yesterday

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting and Finance Minister Song Ziwen Both Attended

Both Sides' Opinions Gradually Approaching

To Continue Discussions in Shanghai Within Days

The Sino-Japanese tariff issue, after repeated negotiations between Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, together with Finance Minister Song Ziwen, and Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Shigemitsu Mamoru, has shown some progress. Yesterday morning at 10:30, another meeting was held at the Foreign Affairs Discussion Society. The Chinese attendees were Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, Finance Minister Song Ziwen, and Xu Mo, Director of the European and American Affairs Department. The Japanese side was represented by Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Shigemitsu Mamoru and Shigemitsu's secretary. The meeting adjourned at 1:30 PM.

The detailed proceedings are recorded below:

Meeting Content

Yesterday morning at 9:45, Foreign Minister Wang arrived at the Foreign Affairs Discussion Society first and immediately telegraphed Shigemitsu to come for discussion quickly. Shigemitsu and others arrived at 10:00, and Song Ziwen also arrived at 10:30, whereupon the formal meeting began. First, the various articles that had been agreed upon in previous discussions were sorted out. Then, the issue of reciprocal tariff rates and the types of reciprocal goods were discussed, with much debate. Regarding the effective period of the agreement, the Japanese side strongly advocated setting it at five years, while the Chinese side strongly advocated shortening it. However, in general, the opinions of both sides were very close.

Wang Zhengting States

After the meeting adjourned, Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting told this newspaper's reporter, "Today's meeting was to discuss the Sino-Japanese tariff issue. The opinions of both sides have gradually approached, but formal signing will still require several more meetings. It is feared that it will be difficult to accomplish this in the shortest period of time. Before I return to Beijing, I may need to convene another meeting in Shanghai. The date has not yet been determined."

Xu Mo's Remarks

This newspaper's reporter visited Mr. Xu Mo at his residence last night and inquired about the meeting's results. According to him, "I am not a designated commissioner for the meeting. My coming to Shanghai this time was a coincidence. Minister Wang invited me to participate, so I am not very clear about the content. The various articles discussed today are roughly the same as the tariff agreements signed with various countries. It is expected that the future Sino-Japanese tariff agreement will not have any special points. As for reciprocal tariff rates, they are very common internationally, and each country has its special goods, so it is impossible to invoke the example of Country B to make demands. As for the types of reciprocal goods, they were not mentioned in the meeting, as this is a matter for specialized commissioners and cannot be resolved hastily. Judging from the situation of today's meeting, it proceeded very smoothly, but formal signing may still require another meeting in Shanghai within days."

Wang Zhengting Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday

Welcoming the Danish Crown Prince

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, accompanied by Xu Mo, Director of the European and American Affairs Department, arrived in Shanghai by night train from Beijing at 7:00 yesterday morning. At 9:45 yesterday morning, Foreign Minister Wang went to the office of the Foreign Affairs Discussion Society on Avenue Joffre. The Sino-Japanese tariff meeting was held at 10:30 (see the above article). He also instructed Chen Shiguang, the director of the office, to purchase a pair of antique vases and several pieces of embroidery as special gifts for the Danish Crown Prince and royal family who are visiting China this time. Foreign Minister Wang also plans to personally greet them at the New Customs Wharf on the morning of the 9th and is scheduled to return to Beijing by train on Monday night next week.

Danish Crown Prince Arrives in Shanghai Tomorrow Morning

Landing at the New Customs Wharf

The Danish Crown Prince and royal family's visit to China arrived in Shanghai on the Fenella ship from Hong Kong on the 6th. They are expected to arrive at Wusongkou at 7:00 tomorrow morning. At that time, the Naval Reorganization Office will dispatch a small steamer to greet them and take them directly to the New Customs Wharf to land. The Foreign Affairs Office sent a letter to the Garrison Headquarters yesterday, requesting that a military band be sent to the wharf to welcome them.

Negotiations to Recover the French Concession Police Headquarters

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is Only Making Preliminary Contact

This newspaper's reporter interviewed an important figure in diplomatic circles yesterday, inquiring about the recent progress in recovering the French Concession Police Headquarters. According to the reply, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has been preparing to recover the French Concession Police Headquarters for a long time, but recently it is still in the stage of preliminary contact. Formal discussions are still far away. When asked whether there has been any recent development in the Sino-French treaty revision negotiations, the reply was that the French side is using the new tax in Guangxi Province as an excuse to delay negotiations. In reality, the signing of the Sino-French commercial treaty is of no benefit to the French side, so they are resorting to all kinds of difficulties and delaying tactics.

Cancellation of the Sino-American Aviation Contract

Direct Negotiations by Wang Boqun

The Results are Quite Good and Can Be Resolved Soon

Regarding the issue of canceling the Sino-American aviation contract, according to reliable sources in diplomatic circles yesterday, it has recently been directly negotiated in Beijing by Wang Boqun, Chairman of the China National Aviation Corporation, and the American Flying Transport Company. The results are quite good and should be resolved in the short term. Because the Flying Transport Company is not operated by the American government, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is only playing a participating role in the negotiations.

Two Railway Party Departments Prepare for the Fifth Anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's Death

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Special Party Departments, taking March 11 as the fifth anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's death, specially invited the two Railway Administrations to hold a preparatory meeting at the department at 2 PM yesterday. The Railway Administration appointed Section Chief Ma of the General Affairs Department as a representative to attend the meeting to discuss the preparatory matters for the commemorative ceremony and to engage in an expanded afforestation movement. It was agreed that the Railway Administration would add saplings and plant them extensively. The address will be held in Nanxiang. The following is a summary of the measures: (1) The public memorial and tree planting ceremony will be held at Nanxiang Station. The time is 10:00 AM on March 12, and the special train will depart at 8:40 AM. (2) The eulogy for the public memorial and tree planting will be handled by the Propaganda Section of the Party Department. (3) Party members who participate in the public memorial and tree planting ceremony must report directly to the General Affairs Section of the Special Party Department, and railway staff must report to the General Affairs Section of the Railway Administration (deadline is 11:00 AM on March 11, starting from the 10th). (4) Black gauze shall be prepared by the party members and staff themselves (size is not limited). (5) Each district party department will only hold public memorials, and staff at all levels will be notified by the Railway Administration to participate nearby. (6) Saplings will be prepared by the Railway Administration. (7) A memorial arch will be arranged as appropriate. (8) Refreshments will be prepared by the Railway Administration. (9) Slogans will be prepared by the Propaganda Section of the Party Department. (10) The venue will be handled by the Propaganda Section of the Party Department and the General Affairs Section of the Railway Administration. (11) The military band will be handled by the Railway Administration. (12) Party songs, etc., will be handled by the Propaganda Section of the Party Department. (13) Photography and other matters will be handled by the Railway Administration. (14) The nameplates for tree planting will be made of bamboo strips and prepared by the Railway Administration. (15) Wreaths will be prepared by the Party Department, etc.

Two District Party Departments Oppose the British Governor's Dissolution of the Nanyang British General Branch

The First and Third District Party Departments of this city, on the grounds that the Party's General Branch stationed in the Nanyang British territories was unreasonably suppressed by Kim Wengon, the British Governor of the area, and ordered to disband. If it fails to abolish and disband within the time limit, the final steps will be taken to deal with it, etc., therefore, a declaration was specially issued yesterday, requesting the central government to seriously negotiate and party departments in various places to oppose it in unison.

Traces of Contemporary Figures

Niu Yongjian, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, arrived in Shanghai yesterday by express train from Zhenjiang and arrived in port that evening.

Li Shizeng, a Supervisory Committee member, left Beijing the night before and arrived in Shanghai by night train yesterday morning.

Sun Ke, Minister of Railways, left Beijing last night for Shanghai and is expected to arrive in port tonight.

Johnson's Speech on the Shanghai Concession Problem

The United Nations Association held a public banquet for Mr. Johnson, the American Minister to China, at its clubhouse on Beijing Road at noon yesterday. More than a hundred Chinese and foreign people attended. Mr. Cunningham, the American Consul General in Shanghai, presided over the meeting and delivered a welcome speech. Minister Johnson gave a reply speech on the topic of the Shanghai Concession Problem, which was the first public speech given by Mr. Johnson since he became Minister to China. The full text of his speech is translated below:

Minister Johnson said, "About eighty years ago, a number of foreign merchants brought goods from their home countries to the Bund to trade with the Chinese. They obtained permission to purchase land and establish businesses. Soon, from residences to offices, from offices to warehouses, and from warehouses to ships, they realized the need for streets, patrolling streets, directing traffic, and providing lighting. From their demands arose the need to cooperate with the local Chinese, because they were the masters of the commercial port. The result of the cooperation between Chinese and foreign merchants was the creation of the most prosperous market in the East. The Shanghai International Settlement stands proudly today, a magnificent memorial arch built through the goodwill cooperation of various nationalities to achieve a common goal. The result of international cooperation is something that both Chinese and foreigners can be proud of, and they feel that it can greatly demonstrate the achievements of business groups working together without the help of the government. It is impossible to limit its importance. It can be said that any enthusiastic person who comes to this place will shout wildly, 'Oh, I never imagined that here, I could witness the supreme grace of internationalism!' Since the cooperation between Chinese and foreigners has created such a monument, in the future, Chinese and foreigners must cooperate to protect and maintain this city. Everyone feels that it is extremely important. Shanghai accounts for a large part of Eastern commerce. People from various countries collect certain taxes in this commerce for transportation costs, water freight, interest, port fees, or tariffs, etc. Once cooperation is stopped, countless people will be overturned. Since merchants gather here, the branches and tributaries will spread widely, and the homes of workers and the mansions of wealthy merchants can be said to be everywhere. And what cannot be ignored most is the impact on the government's tax revenue from the huge commerce passing through this port. The so-called monument to international effort, Shanghai, will succeed with continued cooperation and be destroyed with the cessation of cooperation."

League of Nations Far East Opium Investigation Team Arrives in Shanghai

No Investigation in Shanghai

To Go to Dalian Next Week

The three members of the International League of Nations Far East Opium Investigation Committee, Holck-Larsen, Jurad, and Havlásek, departed from Geneva, passed through India, Annam, the South Seas Islands, and Hong Kong, and arrived in Shanghai yesterday. They will go to Dalian next week. It is heard that these three are passing through Shanghai by chance and have no investigation task.

Organization and Mission

The chief member of the delegation, Holck-Larsen, told this newspaper's reporter yesterday that the delegation was commissioned by the League of Nations and composed of three countries that have no vested interest in the opium issue. He is Swedish, one of the others is Belgian, and one is Czech. Their mission is to go to the invited countries to investigate the situation of opium smoking and trafficking, and report the investigation results to the League of Nations. The League of Nations originally scheduled to hold a ban on opium conference last year, but it has been decided to postpone it to next year to wait for their report. As for how the League of Nations will handle it later, he cannot say on its behalf. They have already passed through India, Annam, Siam, the Dutch East Indies, the South Seas Islands, French Indochina, the Philippines, Japan, Taiwan, and Macau. Because they were not invited in Shanghai, they will not investigate. They are scheduled to go to Dalian, Shenyang, and other places next week.

Anti-Drug Association Does Not Recognize the Visiting Far East Opium Investigation Team

The Opium Advisory Committee of the League of Nations sent personnel to organize the Far East Opium Investigation Team, refusing Chinese representatives to join the investigation, and the scope of the investigation is limited to the Far East, which is greatly unfair in terms of legal principles. The Chinese representative Wang Jingqi, Minister to the Hague, raised objections. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association is even more dissatisfied with the organization of the delegation and has repeatedly opposed it and is planning response methods. The delegation has arrived in Shanghai a few days ago. Yesterday, they specially went to the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association to inquire about the association's views on the delegation's visit to China. The following is a verbatim record of it. The association had previously issued a declaration stating that the scourge of opium and narcotic drugs is spread all over the world. Imperialist countries, such as Britain, Japan, France, the Netherlands, Switzerland, and Germany, have taken it as a tool for economic aggression and the vanguard of military aggression. Because guns and warships can only be used for combat, opium poisons can be used anytime and anywhere by taking advantage of unequal treaties and consular jurisdiction. As a result, not only economic benefits are obtained, but also the country can be destroyed and the people annihilated. It is the most ruthless policy and the most profound crime in the international community. Anyone with a little conscience is heartbroken and eager to find a way to eliminate it and seek a glimmer of life for world humanity. Previously, various countries have repeatedly convened ban conferences, and they have signed conventions and mutually believed in adherence, but in the end, countries that produce opium and narcotics have no sincerity and deceive each other with diplomatic means, causing the scourge of opium to spread and increase day by day. And our country, which has always been contested by the great powers, has become the world's largest market for drugs. The disaster is vast and cannot be cleaned up. Thinking of this, the pain is extreme. In 1924, the League of Nations convened a ban on opium conference, hoping that the sincerity of all countries would be combined to jointly eliminate opium and narcotics. Our people, because of the promotion of the anti-drug movement, thought that there would be international support, but the representatives of Britain, Japan, and other countries only sought the interests of their own opium merchants, disregarded humanity, and were blinded by profit, which resulted in our country's proposal to restrict the manufacture of narcotics not being passed, and blamed our country for producing too much opium, causing it to be the culprit for destroying the world's ban on opium, which caused the meeting to end without results. Recently, the Opium Advisory Committee, based on the suggestion of the British representative, organized the Far East Opium Investigation Team and sent commissioners to our country and various countries in the Far East to investigate the opium situation. Although it has been unanimously opposed by our country from top to bottom, the delegation is still actively coming. Examining its intentions, it is nothing more than seeking evidence of our country's lax opium ban in order to provide a basis for interfering in our country's internal affairs, and to expose our country's inferiority to the world so that our country will become the target of public criticism at next year's international ban on opium conference. Therefore, the area of ​​investigation is limited to the Far East, the scope of investigation is limited to opium, the selection of investigators excludes our country's representatives, and the cost of investigation comes from the League's public funds. What could be more unfair than this? Our association is concerned about national affairs and hates the scourge of drugs. It believes that this investigation is inappropriate. If the League of Nations sincerely intends to eliminate the world's drug scourge, it should adopt fair and stable methods, accommodate our country's opinions, expand the area of ​​investigation to countries all over the world, not just limited to the Far East, the scope of investigation should include narcotics, not just limited to opium, and the organization of the delegation should have our country's representatives join, so that it can be fair. The delegation is still actively coming to China despite our country's opposition. It can be seen that its intentions are ill-conceived and its actions are illegal. In addition to publishing the unfair points of the delegation to the world and exposing the reality of foreign drugs entering China, we deeply hope that compatriots across the country will, on the one hand, urge the government to strictly enforce the opium ban to avoid providing an excuse for foreigners, and on the other hand, resist foreign drugs, expose their policy of harming China and seek world public opinion. The association absolutely does not recognize the delegation's visit to China.

International Exchange Conference Does Not Send Representatives

The International Conference on Uniform Laws for Bills of Exchange, Promissory Notes, and Checks is scheduled to hold a general meeting at the League of Nations in Geneva on May 12 this year. Zhao Jinqing, the Economic Commissioner of the Economic Committee of the conference in China, received a letter from the International Conference requesting that representatives be sent. After the conference sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs requesting that representatives be appointed to attend the meeting, it received a reply from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which stated that this conference is extremely important, but it concerns economics and should be appointed by the Ministry of Finance. However, the Ministry of Finance replied that it is not necessary to send representatives this year and that it will handle it at the next meeting. After receiving the letter, Commissioner Zhao has already sent a letter to the League of Nations for verification.

Zhejiang Provincial Commissioners Set Sail Yesterday

Cheng Zhenjun, a member of the Zhejiang Provincial Government and Director of the Construction Department (it was mistakenly reported in yesterday's newspaper as Director of the Civil Affairs Department), and Liu Yiyan, a specialist member of the National Government's Construction Committee and Deputy Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Bureau, were dispatched by the Zhejiang Provincial Government to visit various European and American countries to investigate construction administration and other important construction matters. They set off on the President Madison of the Dollar Steamship Company on the 7th to Japan. It is heard that they will investigate in Japan for two weeks and then go to the United States, where they will stay for about six weeks, and then transfer from Britain to Belgium, Germany, France, Switzerland, the Netherlands, Italy, Turkey, and other countries. In addition to investigating construction administration, such as organizational systems, material selection, and personnel recruitment, they will also do their best to investigate and study power generation, farmland irrigation, artificial silk, railway factories, and other undertakings. For this trip abroad, Cheng and Liu have been assisted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Zhejiang Provincial Government by sending telegrams to the envoys of various countries, and there have also been considerable contacts with consuls and foreign firms in various countries. Although the investigation period is only five months, the two gentlemen are very familiar with the situation in Europe and America. After returning to China after this investigation, they will definitely make great contributions to the construction undertaking.

New General Manager of Commercial Press, Mr. Wang Yunwu, Goes Abroad for Investigation

Mr. Wang Yunwu has served as the Director of the Compilation and Translation Department of the Commercial Press for a long time. His rich knowledge has long been known to the Chinese people. His greatest contributions in recent years are one, inventing the Four-Corner Code Indexing Method, which has been adopted by no less than one million people at home and abroad within two years, and two, creating and compiling the Complete Library, which has led to the establishment of thousands of new small libraries in various parts of the country within a few months. Mr. Wang resigned from the position of Director of the Compilation and Translation Department of the Commercial Press due to overwork last summer and was appointed Director of the Legal System Group of the Social Science Research Institute of the National Central Research Institute. He is currently engaged in large-scale and thorough research on the issue of crime in our country. Last winter, due to the death of Mr. Bao Xianchang, the General Manager of the Commercial Press, the company's board of directors elected Mr. Wang to succeed him. For several months, Mr. Wang firmly declined, but he agreed to temporarily assume the title and first go to Europe, America, and Japan to investigate everything for about half a year before returning to China to take up the position of General Manager of the Commercial Press. Mr. Wang set off on the President Madison of the Dollar Steamship Company yesterday (the 7th).

Honors of Wu Jingxiong in the United States

Dr. Wu Jingxiong, Dean of the Soochow Law School on Kunshan Road in this port, went to the United States on December 28 last year at the invitation of Northwestern and Harvard Universities. The school received a letter from Dr. Wigmore, Dean of Northwestern University, stating that Mr. Wu arrived in Seattle on January 13 and in St. Paul on the 17th. The Bar Association of the city immediately invited him to give a lecture on the 22nd because of his reputation. He transferred to Chicago. All the Chinese students of the University of Chicago Law School and representatives of the school's Education Department came to the station to welcome him. On the 24th, he gave a lecture at the Department of Political Science of the University of Chicago. On the 25th, the Dean of Northwestern University and the President of the Student Union hosted a public banquet for Mr. Wu and, at the request of Mr. Rosenthal's son, visited the Commercial and Other Courts of Chicago. When the court was hearing a case of international public law, Mr. Wu was present. All the magistrates stood up to pay their respects. After being introduced by the President of the court, Mr. Wu was specially invited to sit with them and observe the trial and consult on everything. This is the first honor that a Chinese person has received in the American judiciary. On the 26th, at the invitation of the Consular Corps of Chicago, he gave a lecture at the Ji Hui Hall of Northwestern University on the topic of Consular Jurisdiction and China. There were representatives from seventeen countries, but the Chinese Consul was the only one absent, which Mr. Wu deeply regretted. On the 27th and 28th, he gave lectures at the Northwestern University Law School. There were more than 600 professors, magistrates, and students in attendance. Mr. Wu's topics were one, Ancient Chinese Jurisprudence, and two, a Comparison of the Old and New Legal Systems of China. Mr. Wu criticized Chinese and foreign legal systems with a philosophical perspective and summarized the evolution of law in China for thousands of years into a coherent chapter, which he instilled in the minds of tens of thousands of people in two hours. Mr. Wei called it a model speech and the same success as Professor Howeiss's lecture at the school three years ago. Mr. Wu's remarks are regarded as treasures by the American press. His speeches are published in local newspapers and benefit tens of thousands of people. If he can give more lectures at various American societies, it will surely increase American goodwill towards China. Finally, he said that the Northwestern University Library intends to compile a book on the History of Chinese Legal System and asked Dr. Sheng Zhenwei to collect materials on his behalf and expressed his gratitude. According to the Northwestern University Law School's Rosenthal Foundation Lecture Series, it was donated by the great industrialist Rosenthal and is specially used to invite world legal scholars to give lectures. Mr. Wu was selected for this, which is the only glory for our East Asia.

Japanese Aircraft Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon

To Fly Back to Fukuoka Tomorrow Morning

The Shanghai news of the Japanese News Alliance on the 7th, the Sino-Japanese liaison test flight by the Japan Air Transport Company from Fukuoka to Shanghai, was extended by two days due to the hurricane. Today, it was finally held. Although the weather was not good, the first test flight has been completed. The pilot Fujimoto and five staff members took a Dornier seaplane (which can seat twelve people) and departed from Fukuoka Meijima Airport at 7:49 AM (Shanghai time) and flew over Tomie, Goto at 9:13 AM. They landed on the Yangshupu water surface at 12:38 PM. The flight distance was 950 kilometers, the speed per hour was 107 knots, and the flight time was 4 hours and 51 minutes. This time it was a test flight and there were no passengers. It is scheduled to depart from Shanghai at 8:00 AM on the 9th and fly back to Fukuoka. The pilot Fujimoto said, "This morning at 6:00, we received weather reports from Jeju Island and Tomie saying that there were clouds but no rain in the Shanghai area, so we flew. When we passed Tomie, we encountered heavy rain, followed by headwinds of 10 to 15 meters. Because the dense clouds were too low, the plane could only fly 200 meters above the sea surface. If there was no wind, the flight time should be 5 and a half hours. Because we were flying with the wind, we were able to shorten the time by one and a half hours. We saw three ships along the way. This plane has no danger to life, so the driving is quite enjoyable."

Municipal Government Orders the Social Affairs Bureau to Crack Down on Profiteering Merchants Hoarding Grain

Instructing the Public Safety Bureau to Order Strict Enforcement

The Municipal Government, in order to comply with orders to crack down on profiteering merchants hoarding grain and to maintain the people's food supply, has specifically instructed the Social Affairs Bureau as follows: "For the matter of issuing instructions, a document No. 177 from the Ministry of Interior Affairs has been approved, stating that it is a matter for requesting instructions. A directive No. 311 from the Executive Yuan was received, which stated, 'A document No. 473 from the Secretariat of the National Government was approved, stating that a letter from the Central Political Council concerning the Executive Yuan's report on the food problem and the proposed measures by various departments has been received. The meeting of this council has resolved to approve the measures proposed by the Ministry of Interior Affairs regarding the crackdown on profiteering merchants. Please forward this for compliance and a response.' An edict was received instructing the Executive Yuan to forward this for compliance. In addition to replying to the letter, a copy of the original document is enclosed to be forwarded for your information and action.' This has been approved. Apart from replying to the letter for submission and issuing separate orders to the Ministry of Finance, the original documents and attachments are hereby copied and issued, instructing the relevant departments to comply and report separately." This has been received. Upon investigation, this case was previously submitted to the Executive Yuan for deliberation, and it was determined that to crack down on profiteering merchants smuggling grain for export, the Ministry of Finance should first issue a general order to customs to strictly prohibit it. Regarding the crackdown on profiteering merchants hoarding grain and the prevention of improper grain consumption, it was proposed that this department instruct the provinces and halls to strictly crack down based on local conditions, and a request for review was submitted. Now, in accordance with the aforementioned reasons, in addition to replying and issuing separate instructions, a document is hereby sent to your government for review and instruction to your subordinates to strictly crack down to maintain the people's food supply, and to report the crackdown measures for reference." This has been approved. It is hereby ordered that the bureau, in conjunction with the Public Safety Bureau, instruct its subordinates to strictly crack down and report the crackdown measures for verification and onward transmission. This order.

Agreed Measures for County Public Safety Expenses

The Shanghai County public safety expenses have been in a state of limbo for a long time, with no solution. Therefore, the county government convened a meeting of the heads of various bureaus and districts under the county yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM in the county government conference hall to discuss raising regular expenses for the county Public Safety Bureau. Over a dozen people, including County Head Leng, attended. Leng Jun chaired the meeting, and Hu Gongshou served as the recorder. The meeting proceeded according to protocol. After the chairman's report, discussion began. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Attendees: County Head Leng Jun, Secretary Fan Shuhan, Section Chief Xu Xiaochu of the First Section, Section Chief Qian Tingbi of the Second Section, Public Safety Shen Jinghua, Finance Li Zuyong, Zhang Pengfei, Jiang Lichuan of the Property Office, Yang Fulin of the Second District, Bi Huan of the Fourth District, Ren Yongkang of the Fifth District, and eleven others.

Report Items: After the meeting proceeded according to protocol, the chairman gave a report, stating, "The county's public safety expenses have been in a state of limbo for a long time, and the difficulties are indescribable. Today's meeting is convened to ask everyone to jointly discuss measures to fundamentally solve this most urgent problem." After the chairman's report, Public Safety Bureau Chief Shen Jinghua reported, stating, "The establishment of the police is to maintain the local area. Expenses should also be allocated on time. Shanghai is a place where Chinese and foreigners mix, and the population is diverse. The issue of defense is extremely important. Our bureau and its subordinate branches have only about 200 officers and police in total. It is already difficult to maintain the county's security with this number. Moreover, the monthly salary of the officers and police is only half that of the Municipal Bureau. Life is particularly difficult. Recently, there has been no funding at all, and we are on the verge of starvation. The monthly regular expenses for the county and the four branch bureaus total more than 3,920 yuan. In the past, the municipal government allocated funds from the city's property tax revenue each month according to the amount. Since June of last year, the allocation has been stopped, and the public safety expenses have suddenly become unavailable. County Head Leng has repeatedly transferred funds from other sources to provide some relief. Recently, all resources have been exhausted and there is no way to continue. Only half of the salary for January of this year has been paid, and the salary for February is overdue. If measures are not taken urgently, it will be impossible to support it. In total, the annual regular expenses for our bureau and the four branch bureaus are about 47,000 yuan. The cost of clothing and temporary expenses is about 7,300 yuan. The annual total is 54,300 yuan. Jinghua has not been in office for long and is unfamiliar with the people and the place. To seek remedies, I rely on everyone's efforts. What measures should be taken to first raise the arrears and then pay the salaries on a monthly basis to eliminate this problem?"

Resolutions: Resolutions on measures to raise regular expenses for the Public Safety Bureau: (1) In accordance with the resolutions of the first and second administrative meetings, property tax should be reorganized. The county government should immediately send personnel to conduct a thorough investigation of the actual rents, verify the tax amount, together with the district chiefs and public safety branch chiefs. (2) The county head and the Public Safety Bureau chief should submit a report to the provincial government and the municipal government to liquidate the accounts and consult with the municipal government to continue the allocation as before. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Defense After the End of the Winter Defense Period

Instructions from the Garrison Headquarters

The Songhu Garrison Command recently issued instructions to its military and police agencies, stating that although the winter defense period has ended, the situation is still unstable, rumors are rampant, and Shanghai is a place where Chinese and foreigners mix and there are many bandits. The defense should not be relaxed. The instructions stated: "For the matter of issuing instructions, given the current unstable situation and the lurking of bandits, although the winter defense period has ended, in order to ensure thorough security, all military and police should continue to maintain strict vigilance in accordance with the plans and procedures stipulated in the winter defense plan. They should also pay attention to reconnaissance of bandit and reactionary activities in various places, prevent and suppress them at any time, and report on the handling of these matters for verification and instruction. This is imperative."

Japan's Trade Statistics with China for February

Excess of Exports of 16 Million Yuan

2 Million Yuan Less Than Last Year

According to the Japanese Embassy's Commercial Affairs Office, Japan's total trade with China in February of this year was 33 million yuan, with an excess of exports of 16 million yuan. Dispute over the 加佣案 of the Yuye Dunhe Gongsuo

Fish Merchants Object...Social Affairs Bureau Orders the Gongsuo to Respond

The practice of the Shanghai Fish Market to sell goods on behalf of customers has been to take a commission of seven cents per yuan, plus dock labor and other fees. After adding a commission of one cent in the 15th year of the Republic of China, the company this February requested the Social Affairs Bureau to add another one-cent commission to make up for the losses of previous years. The Social Affairs Bureau retrieved the expenditure accounts of the company to investigate the matter. It was later found that the company had lost about 20,000 yuan in the 18th year, so it was approved. It was also ordered to withdraw two li from the increased commission and deposit it in a special account for the construction of docks and cold storage, and to pay for the public welfare and charitable undertakings of the fishermen. Recently, it was heard that the fish merchants were unable to bear the burden and filed a petition with the Social Affairs Bureau, asking for the cancellation of the commission increase and requesting an investigation of the Dunhe Gongsuo's accounts over the years. The Social Affairs Bureau has ordered the Gongsuo to provide a clear response within a time limit for further verification.

What We Heard After the Election of Foreign Directors of the 工部局

British and American Concessions – The Question

The Reason for Arnold's Resignation

A Certain Japanese Person Expresses Their Opinion

The Shanghai Times reported: "Since the results of this year's election of foreign directors of the 工部局 were announced, the British have taken six seats, while the Americans have only taken one. It has been said that one of the newly elected British directors will resign to allow the next-highest American to fill the seat. However, according to someone who knows the 工部局 well, this matter, if it can benefit the public on the British side, at least one person will be willing to resign voluntarily to give way to the American. However, whether this can become a reality is still difficult to say. It is also said that it has not yet been formally discussed at the board meeting." A certain important American figure stated that this proposal is indeed in the spirit of sportsmanship on the British side, and it is admirable to give way. However, for the Americans, accepting this proposal would inevitably mean losing the spirit of sportsmanship. The reason why only one American was elected this time is because there were three candidates, and the votes were split, resulting in two people not being elected. According to a certain gentleman of the 工部局, within this year, perhaps one of the British directors will resign for some reason, and at that time, an American will likely fill the vacancy.

After the British Arnold resigned as Director-General, he sent a letter to various Western newspapers yesterday, stating the reasons for his defeat and resignation, stating: "As Director-General, he was unable to fully agree to the Japanese's increased requests for Japanese police and other matters. Therefore, in the days before the election, he knew that he could only get 200 votes out of the 600 Japanese voters. If the election results were as expected, the Westerners would have cast more than 510 votes for him. He heard that 90% of the Japanese voters went to the polls, while only 50% of the British did. If the British expatriates continue to abandon their right to vote, the election of foreign directors will be dominated by the Japanese expatriates. However, since many new figures have been elected this time, perhaps the citizens will pay more attention to municipal affairs than before. During his tenure, he improved the municipal hospital and nursing system, improved the living conditions of Chinese and Western police, thoroughly reformed the Chinese Education Department, began to eliminate the old and promote the younger members of the 工部局 staff, gradually increased the employment of Chinese staff, and organized a salary committee to consider salary issues. In addition, he organized a bureau member association to coordinate the relationship between the board of directors and the bureau members, and improved the entire education system to give Chinese and foreign children equal opportunities. He strongly advocated hiring experts to investigate telephones and firmly rejected the request of the China & Foreign Telephone Company to accept the contract of the American capital group, asking them to openly bid. In addition, such matters as harmonizing Chinese-foreign relations, sending Fei Xin悙 to Nanjing to attend the Pacific Conference, and hiring Gu Fei Tang as a consultant are all major achievements of the past year. Since the voters do not approve of this policy, it will be difficult for the board of directors if he continues to guide the formulation of the new policy for this year in the coming weeks. Therefore, he is resigning early."

A Wenhui Bao reporter met with a certain respected Japanese taxpayer in this port and asked about Arnold's letter published in various Western newspapers. The Japanese person denied the claim that the Japanese expatriates had assigned votes before the election and said, "Since Mr. Arnold's political views were not satisfactory to the Japanese expatriates, why would they give him 200 votes? Moreover, the Japanese would never be so foolish as to foreshadow his rejection of someone he was dissatisfied with. Moreover, the increase of Japanese police is a trivial matter. If it is said that this affected the election, isn't that a joke? It is heard that the proposal to increase Japanese police did not come from the Japanese directors. The increased Japanese police have already been transported from Japan as originally planned." The Japanese person also criticized some newspapers for advocating that a British director give up a seat so that a certain American who was not elected could fill the vacancy, saying that this move was enough to cause sadness.
