Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Hai Ke

Doctor: Your illness is completely cured. What you need is exercise. You need to walk one or two li every day, and it must be with a purpose.

Patient: Doctor, I will definitely do as you say. I will definitely walk one or twenty li every day. My purpose is to visit relatives and old friends one by one, and borrow money to pay your huge medical bill.

Man: I love how delicate and timid you are. You're afraid as soon as you see a dog. So are you afraid when you see a cow?

Woman (blushing): I don't have that experience. Because my father is the boss of a dairy farm. When I see a cow, it's like seeing a lover.

Editor A: This article of yours needs to be clearer, I'm afraid people without knowledge will not understand it.

Editor B: Then point out to me which part you don't understand.

A: Can you lend me a hundred yuan? I can return it in just one week.

B: I'm also short on funds these days. I only have fifty yuan.

A: Then lend me fifty yuan. But it has to be extended to two weeks to return. This is your own fault.

Gandhi in the Mouth of an American

— Zhi Zheng

The famous American sociologist, Mr. Page, has come to China and has given speeches at the YMCA, which have been well-received by the general public. Yesterday, he was also invited to Jiaotong University to speak about the Indian sage Gandhi. He spoke highly of Gandhi, and here's what I remember.

Gandhi's appearance, Mr. Page said, Gandhi was short and weighed less than one hundred pounds. His clothes were very simple, and his appearance was ordinary. He did not eat rice or vegetables every day, he only ate a few pieces of fruit.

A world-class great man, he said, Gandhi studied in England in his early years. After returning to his country, he practiced law. One day, he represented a client in court, but he stuttered repeatedly during his speech and eventually left the stage red-faced. His embarrassment at the time can be imagined. After this stimulus, he devoted himself to learning even more. Gandhi, based on his life's work, was truly a great politician, a social reformer, and a saint. To be all three at once, can he not be called a world-class great man?

India's young widows. Early marriage is a custom in India. Children are married off at the age of four or five. After the husband dies, regardless of the wife's age, she cannot remarry. Therefore, there are quite a few Indian women who are young widows at the age of four or five. The destruction of women's happiness has reached this extreme. Gandhi shouted loudly, arousing people's attention to this matter. To this day, this trend has been slightly curbed, it is said.

The power of non-violent resistance. Non-violent resistance was created by Gandhi. One year, the British government ordered the Indians to submit fingerprints. Gandhi ordered the people not to go. Thousands of people were arrested. The prisons were full. The authorities were terrified. After the Indian people were released, they still refused to submit. The British were eventually helpless. Gandhi's advocacy of passive resistance against the British particularly emphasized economic severance. Therefore, the British forces in India were greatly hit by Gandhi. Today, Gandhi even sent a letter of protest to the Indian Governor, implementing his non-violent resistance. Its momentum can be known.

A stone from another mountain. After Mr. Page finished his speech, the audience responded with enthusiastic applause. Gandhi, as a citizen of a subjugated country, led the masses, implemented economic severance with non-cooperation, and eventually made the British submit. People in our country, who are also in a semi-colonial situation, hear this and cannot remain unmoved. The lecture of Mr. Page probably contains a deep meaning.

A Record of the Female Bandit Who Sold Entertainment

— Lü Bing

The old servant Ya Ci came from Huzhou. He told me that it was very difficult to travel to Huzhou. Because today, bandits are everywhere. There are direct steamships from Shanghai to Huzhou. But a month ago, they were robbed several times. Timid people regard it as a dangerous road. They changed to take the Shanghai-Hangzhou train to Jiaxing, and then take a boat to Huzhou. The mileage is faster. Unexpectedly, this Jiaxing bus was also looted in the previous ten days. The losses were quite heavy, and the journey was full of thorns. He said with fear. Ya Ci lives in the countryside, close to Taihu Lake. He mentioned two female bandits in Taihu Lake, who are extremely fierce. What he said is credible.

Taihu Lake has crisscrossing harbors and channels, which are not navigable by those unfamiliar with the routes. Over the years, many bandits have gathered in between. Most of them are from the Hunan gang and the Jiangbei gang. Thatched houses are hidden, and fishing boats are hidden. This is the easiest place to hide. However, the heroes of the green forest are all strong men. Even if there is a "wife in the stronghold," she has never shown her face. It was not until last year when Wucheng and Erzhen were ravaged by bandits that two female bandits were seen. They held box cannons and directed things. So the residents paid attention. It is said that there are female bandits in Taihu Lake. According to residents of Taihu Lake, one of the female bandits is about thirty years old, and the other is less than thirty. They wear short clothes and foot bindings, cut their hair short, and wear hats. The older one is fierce and terrifying. The younger one has a decent face. She used to be a female entertainer, traveling through the border between Zhejiang and Jiangsu, earning money by performing acrobatics. The villagers in Xunzhen still have vague memories of her. It is unknown how she became a bandit. The female bandits are agile and walk very fast. They speak with a Shandong accent. They also drive boats in Taihu Lake from time to time. The fishermen in Taihu Lake point them out whenever they meet them. Since the Zhejiang provincial authorities have been searching and suppressing them strictly, the bandits have recently subsided slightly.

New Discussion on Rat Extermination

— Ji Jin

The Ta Kung Pao reported the other day that in a house in Taiheng Lane, North Sichuan Road, in this city, a mother and child were both bitten by rats. It was later reported to the Bureau of Health, which tried to search and arrest them, but only caught two or three small rats. The larger ones escaped, fearing future troubles. I say that the harm caused by rats exists everywhere. I have never heard of anyone being seriously injured by a rat bite. Now I will discuss the art of rat extermination with my friends, and briefly record it below to inform the readers.

Western methods of rat extermination are countless. Generally, stores, households, and ships must spray toxic gas once every three months to avoid the occurrence of nuclear plague, ringworm, rat malaria, rat plague, and various diseases. This is of course perfect. I do not know that rats are very cunning, coming and going suddenly, and unpredictable. There are even those who board ships to cross the ocean, and those who take cars to go to foreign countries. Recently, small mice have been found in airplanes in some places in the United States. What a strange thing. Everyone knows that their reproduction is very fast. One female rat can give birth about six times a year, about five or six at a time. According to the world's statistical report, there are currently more than nine thousand trillion rats. Extermination is endless, what to do?

According to a recent Western magazine, London, England, initiated a city-wide rat extermination conference. It is scheduled to be held simultaneously on a certain day of a certain month, and a rat extermination liquid will be sprayed by machine. This liquid contains an excessively strong irritant, which makes the rats feel feverish all over when they smell it. They want to die but cannot. They leave their burrows and seek shade. When they encounter cold air, the poison is released and they die immediately. It will never rot in the burrow and cause a rat plague. This medicine is called Cogesters water. It was invented by Dr. Cogesters of the Royal Hospital, so it is named after him. It is said that the test is effective and will be sold to various countries so that rats will be exterminated.

New Couplet

— Lai

Madame Wu, the former president of Lebanon, passed away a few days ago. Mr. Li Genyuan, the former Prime Minister of Lebanon, is currently living in seclusion in the Qionglong Mountains of Suzhou. He specially made a couplet to mourn her, which he sent. "Who in the eyes is like Madame? I still remember the country's many difficulties. In Zhai clothing and hairpin, she diligently warned at dawn. If you meet the President in heaven, tell her that I am safe and sound in the mountains, and I miss her for a long time in the wind and rain of the green lamp." Signed as "The Spiritual Banner of Madame Wu, the Great President." Respectfully mourned by Li Genyuan.

Continued Record of Zhang Fei's Head

— Chen Shuping

Previously, this publication published a section about Zhang Fei's head in the Shu Temple, which attracted the attention of readers. Everyone wants to know the truth in detail. Pharmacist Zhang Jun Yongxiang is a man who is well-versed in the world, knowledgeable, and sincere. He has the air of a Confucian scholar. He came to Shanghai from Sichuan. Last night, I met him at the banquet and immediately asked him about this matter. According to his confirmed account, the temple placed a huge vat in the center of the main hall, filled with cooking oil. The so-called head of Zhang Fei is immersed in it. A thin chain is attached to the end of the hair, which hangs down from the pulley in the beam. Visitors who want to see it must first pay a certain amount of incense money, and then the monk will use the chain to bring out the head. Only a round object wrapped in oiled paper can be seen, as big as a watermelon. There are many official seals on the paper. A black halberd beard is slightly exposed at the lower end. Judging from the beard, the horror of its appearance can be imagined. The monk said that the head was once publicly exhibited, waiting with round eyes and a swallow's jaw, as fierce as alive. Children who saw it were often frightened and became ill, or even died. The local officials then prohibited it from being shown to people. An edict was issued to wrap it up to avoid causing trouble again. Is the Third General not worshipped as a god by the world? However, the most important part of his remains is not buried in the yellow earth, but floats in oil. Is it blasphemy or respect? This is a question. If it is said that it is imitating the preservation methods of the Western museums, the reason is difficult to establish. One is that our country's customs are very different from those of the West. We have always valued the view of being buried in the earth. Except for the Ming Dynasty's punishment of death, there is no precedent for hanging one's head high to show respect. Moreover, a century ago, people still lacked this new idea, especially in the closed province of Sichuan where transportation was inconvenient. Or, it is said that this is a trick by the monks to collect money, and there is no value in research. I don't know if it is true. I hope that the comrades in that place can conduct a detailed investigation using scientific methods and make an accurate report. I believe it is also what the readers would like to hear.

Ping notes that the head has been discovered for a long time. Although the exact date cannot be verified, it must be at least over a hundred years old. Therefore, "a century ago" refers to the day when the temple was exhibited to the public. However, how the monks obtained it is a big question.

Random Talk on Making Letter Paper

— Zhang Zhenlü

In recent years, I have been engaged in the business of making letter paper. Fortunately, the three words "Liang Chen Jian" have been widely accepted by the people. Adopted by each other. Last year, I wrote "Random Talk on Making Letter Paper" based on what I learned from making letter paper and published it in this newspaper. The other day, a guest came to Qingtan. Making letter paper is the way. He left in the middle of the night. I suddenly felt lonely and recorded a note to serve as my footprint.

If a craftsman wants to do his job well, he must first sharpen his tools. Making letter paper is a trivial matter. The words and paintings must be free from vulgarity as the minimum condition. Whether the printing plate is made of zinc or copper, clarity is the most important. If you use movable type to arrange lines and grids, you must use good materials. However, new lead lines have edges that are too sharp due to the edge. Light printing does not leave traces. Heavy printing may break thin paper. Copper wire is better because it is more durable. The printing plate may be the edge of a book. New book edges may have defects in the casting process that cause sand holes. The print looks like pinholes. Old materials are out of the question. Or arrange flower borders, or because the size of the body is too big or too small compared to the planned size of the printing plate. It is too much or too little, and cannot be exactly right. Or because the alignment of the patterns is not accurate, the skilled worker uses his brain to seek a seamless match. The time spent is immeasurable. There are wired printing plates and special printing plates. Zinc and copper printing plates have wooden supports, which are larger than the printing surface. When the characters and paintings on the printing surface are printed, they are far away from the lines and grids, and are not in the Chinese style. Then the skilled worker must use his brain again, or file the edge of the wooden bottom, or cut the bottom of the lead wire, or arrange the lead material vertically and horizontally to maintain it, or line it with thin paper or thick paper to stabilize it. The time spent is immeasurable again. Once the printing plate is ready, the quality of the printing press is another important key to making letter paper. The softness, hardness, expansion, and contraction of the ink glue, the thickness, thinness, and gloss of the ink are all obstacles to printing. The height of the bottom of the printing plate and the flatness of the machine surface are matters for the printing workers. The printing matters are ready. The quality of the paper material, whether it is suitable for this printing plate or not, whether it is suitable for this ink or not, must also be considered. The uniformity of the paper edge is enough to ruin the beauty of the entire letter paper. Therefore, if a craftsman wants to do his job well, he must first sharpen his tools. Although the tools are sharp, the craftsman must also be skilled. Making letter paper is a trivial matter. The difficulty is like this. How can hundreds of industries not be like this? Zhu Bailu has said, "Every thread and every strand, we must always remember that material resources are hard-won." It is indeed worth remembering.

Nanfeng Orange

— Zhi Zheng

Nanfeng County in Jiangxi Province is the hometown of the ancient prose writer Zeng Zigou. The world calls Zeng Nanfeng Mr. Zeng, just like today's Duan Hefei and Zhang Nantong. Nanfeng is not a prosperous place, but the "Nanfeng Orange" is its specialty. Its shape is extremely small, only about one-fifth of the size of those sold on the market. It looks like a lotus coin and is pleasing to the eye. When the skin is removed and eaten, it tastes extremely sweet. The smaller it is, the better it tastes. Therefore, one can easily eat dozens of them at a time. To choose the large ones when buying Nanfeng oranges will surely be laughed at by those in the know. Many farmers in the area grow this. However, because the demand is wide, it is no longer available above Nanchang, let alone Xunhu. My friend Tan Jun Zanhua came to Shanghai from Jiangxi in the new year, bringing a basket of Nanfeng oranges, about hundreds of them. He shared them with his friends, who liked their unique flavor. Therefore, I occasionally talked about it.

Warmth in the Heart (143)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Nine: Celebrated Figures Hilariously Play Hide-and-Seek; A Charming Lady Voluntarily Provides Protection

Speaking of hide-and-seek. Ruiyun was also very enthusiastic. Speaking of hide-and-seek...we must think of the time at the Mingjing Club. That time can be regarded as a large-scale game of hide-and-seek. Among the men...there were Xiong Pingshan, Yi Hu'an, Zhang Junheng, Shi Guanping, Yan Yichen, Zheng Yanxiu, Zuo Shichen, Zhen Cuixia, etc. Among the women...there were Zhao Yuxiang, Yiqing Xian Guan, Shi Yunlai, Hong Sibao, Su Jun, Chen Jiangyun, Hua Ruiyun, etc. It can also be regarded as extremely lively. Among this group of people...later, there were those who became Prime Ministers, those who became Ministers of Departments, and those who became Presidents of Banks. Among the women, most of them were probably girls from the brothel, or mostly concubines of others. But after twenty years, looking back...everyone who attended that night of hide-and-seek is still alive. However, among the men...the young have become middle-aged, and the middle-aged have become old. Those with bare chins have grown beards. Among the women, they have naturally gradually changed from slim young ladies to aging courtesans. But the laughter, the tinkling of pearls, and the chaos of hairpins at that time are worth remembering. At that time, among this group of girls, the most active were Yiqing and Yunlai. Ruiyun was also very active at home...but when she came outside...she was not very good at making noise. After all, she was too young...she did not have the sophistication of Yiqing and Yunlai. The game of hide-and-seek...was also initiated by Yiqing and others. She said, "When I was a child, I was the naughtiest, and I was the best at kicking shuttlecocks and jumping rope. At first, my mother wanted to bind my feet...she bound them tightly during the day...and I didn't feel anything. But at night...when I got hot, my bound feet hurt even more. I didn't care, and I tore off the foot bindings in the quilt. When my mother saw that I didn't cry in pain...she was a little suspicious...she ran over and lifted the quilt to take a look...a quilt full of foot bindings...like a new batch of beltfish arriving from Ningbo...a pair of feet were exposed outside...she was so angry that she wanted to beat me with a chicken feather duster. Fortunately, my father said...in the middle of the night...hitting a child...disturbing the neighbors...what are you doing? Now many young ladies in mansions don't bind their feet...and there are Tianzu Associations everywhere...so just let it be. My mother said...young ladies in mansions don't have to bind their feet...but we small families cannot do without foot binding." She scolded my father...but in the end, she let it go. Once my feet were not bound...it was much more comfortable. When playing hide-and-seek...no one can catch me. Yan Yichen laughed and said...such an old person...still like a child...only talking about hide-and-seek. Yiqing said...what's so strange about that? We played this game with a few younger sisters the night before last. Yunlai echoed her and said...hide-and-seek depends on being physically active...so that you are not caught by others. If you are dull...it won't work. Shi Guanping was also a person who liked excitement...he said...are you playing hide-and-seek? You can play it here.

Financial Gold Rush Aftermath Unsettled

Large Bar Shrinking Again...Heavily Breaking the 500 Taels Mark

Tax News Spreads Again...Falling a Miserable Six Taels; Fluctuations Are as High as Eight Taels. Yesterday, the Gold Market Again Presented a Confusing and Uncertain Situation. With Fluctuations as High as Eight Taels Throughout the Day, and Foreign Exchange Shifting from Tight to Loose, Speculators Sold, and Public Sentiment Was Uneasy. As the Large Bar Shrinking Began in the Early Market, It Opened High. At Noon, Buyers Swarmed in, at Around 503 Taels. Bank of England replenishes… US-Japan trade limited

Yesterday, the exchange rates quoted by HSBC were the same as the day before. Major banks slightly reduced their positions, and exchange rates rose slightly. Recent Overview of the Sanpin Exchange

Arbitration and Special Appraisal of Yarn and Flower Quality

Are Both Solved Accurately with Scientific Instruments

The Osaka Sanpin Exchange, which primarily deals in cotton yarn and cotton futures, gets its name "Sanpin" from the three commodities it was originally intended to trade: cotton, yarn, and cotton cloth. Later, only yarn transactions remained, but two years ago, raw cotton trading resumed. Raw cotton trading is based on 7/8-inch Strict Middling and the standard is strict. SuictMidlio of a quarter of a dan is the basis, and the unit is 10 bales of American cotton (i.e., 36 dan). The standard for cotton yarn is Toyo Cotton Factory's 20-count Goldfish brand, which was decided by the Exchange's Board of Directors in 1927. Each month, the Standards Committee appraises the standard quality of each factory's cotton yarn once, and determines the differential amount to be added or subtracted above or below the standard. Furthermore, if there are differences of opinion regarding the determination of cotton or cotton yarn standards, the Exchange has instruments that measure quality based on scientific principles to make a determination. These instruments are also used in cases of arbitration. The Exchange's rules stipulate that futures trading in cotton or cotton yarn must be conducted using auction methods. However, delivery procedures can be used when specially specified or deemed necessary. In the auction market, brokers must report the price and the quantity they wish to buy or sell. All such trading quantities are temporarily recorded in the market transaction register, and the two parties continue to negotiate prices until the average price of all trades is determined. However, purchases and sales made by the same broker are deemed to offset each other unless specifically stated.

Art World

Artists and the Masses

— Baoluo Duo

Every individual within the masses asks for very little from life within the crowd—merely the right to survive. If anything obstructs their right to survive, they have no choice but to revolt. The revolt of the masses is, in fact, a very justified action. Therefore, in our history, all major disturbances since ancient times should be celebrated as the majority's demand for the right to survive. Regarding this point, even the sage-like figures among the scholar-officials who specialized in suppressing mass movements understood it clearly. For the sake of governing the country and bringing peace to the world, a tendency towards a frugal and simple life naturally arose among Chinese scholar-officials. As a result, all magnificent and ornate decorations were rejected, and culture centered on artistic thought was extremely despised. Because of this, every artist under traditional Chinese thought has always been subjected to unexpected maltreatment. As long as one lived a frugal and simple life, from the emperor (the most famous being Emperor Wen of Han) to the common people, they were all praised. Even in the past ten years or so, despite the fundamental shaking of all previous Chinese thought, those who live a frugal and simple life are still praised. The enjoyment of life centered on artistic thought is something that people in the crowd dare not openly proclaim. Therefore, in our China, there are at least two kinds of life forms: one that can be told to others, and another that cannot. Moreover, under traditional Chinese thought, the latter is unnecessary. Since the life of every artist is naturally different from that of every individual in the masses, then the life of every artist is one that does not need to be told to others. As for the life that the majority demands, it is always very modest—merely the desire to survive. Everything is something that can be told to others, and after others hear it, they will never express dissatisfaction because of it. In short, in a country that worships art, the life of an artist that everyone praises is one that does not need to be told to others in China. Otherwise, they will be subjected to considerable insults, forcing them to come out and deny it in the newspaper. Under such traditional thought, every artist in China who aspires to further their development is still forced to accept everything centered on a frugal and simple life. They are frugal in their enjoyment and monotonous in their lives. In the end, none of them has the life of an artist that everyone praises in a country that worships art.

The life of every artist will never conflict with the life of every individual in the masses.

After most people wake up at dawn, many of their actions are naturally the same as others. Let's list a few of the most important ones below—dressing and eating go without saying. In addition, there is definitely a fixed job every day (of course, washing the face and the like are not included). Living like this day after day, over time, everyone will feel that life is too boring when they are about to die. Every artist should attach great importance to the enjoyment of life. The reason why life is interesting is all because artists shout it out. However, the daily dressing, washing the face, eating, and other fixed jobs are all lives that can be told to others.

Let me say a few blunt words, "One person's waste may be a sin, but a nation's waste should be a cultural enjoyment."

Finally, I would like to say, "As long as it is an excellent nation, there is no lack of waste and squandering in the enjoyment of life. However, this situation is unlikely to happen in China."

Writers and Their Remuneration

— Moli

Everyone knows that the most expensive manuscripts now belong to former US President Coolidge and Governor Smith. Publishers offered a reward of one yuan per word, asking them to write about their personal experiences in politics and society. As a result, Coolidge's six-month writing career earned him more than his annual salary as president (according to British newspapers).

A fee of one yuan per word is indeed considerable, but it cannot be said to be unprecedented. In foreign countries, there are actually many precedents. Several years ago, a scholar from Indiana in the United States, named Whitcomb Riley, wrote a poem called "An Old Sweetheart of Mine." The initial reward for this poem was extremely meager, just a drop in the bucket of his income at the time. But year after year, the number of people reading his poem gradually increased. So, the scenes described in the poem were also painted by very famous artists, creating many beautiful and moving pictures. In this way, his poem "An Old Sweetheart of Mine" almost became a poem that everyone must read. Before his death, the reward he received from that poem was almost five hundred yuan per word. What an astonishing number!

This can be regarded as the highest reward in writing. However, there are many other precedents that prove that poetry can also be rewarded. Alexander Pope translated Homer's epic "Iliad" and received 50,000 yuan. Before Sir Walter Scott became famous for his novels, he was already a "poet" who galloped in the literary world at that time. His popular long poem "Lady of the Lake" received a reward of 15,000 yuan. Also, the British publisher Sir Smith paid 25,000 yuan to have Tennyson write a poem as long as "Idylls of the King". But compared to that, Milton's "Paradise Lost" received a total of only fifty yuan. This amount is too far apart.

The above is mostly the luck of writers. However, on the other hand, there are also many frustrated ones. Edgar Allan Poe was satisfied with getting ten yuan for a short story. Thomas Carlyle's most proud year in his life, his literary earnings were less than a thousand yuan. Beatrice Harraden wrote a novel "Ships That Pass in the Night" and immediately sold it for a hundred yuan. Who knew that after it was published, sales were booming, creating an opportunity for booksellers to make a fortune out of thin air.

But now, this unfair treatment seems to have been eliminated. We are very happy to know how Conan Doyle, who wrote the Sherlock Holmes detective novels, went from poverty to wealth. The year Sherlock Holmes first appeared, which was also the year Conan Doyle first wrote detective novels, was 1887. That novel was called "A Study in Scarlet," and it was 25,000 words long. At that time, the author was still a medical student struggling with his environment. Before it was published, he encountered many difficulties, almost causing him to destroy his manuscript. It was not until someone bought the manuscript that he received a reward of 125 yuan. However, this amount was already much higher than what he used to get from people's random donations. In the first eight or nine years of his writing career, he often wrote late into the night without stopping, but he did not earn eight or nine hundred yuan in any year. Now, the situation is different from before. The copyright for "Sir Nigel" sold for 25,000 yuan. Since then, Sherlock Holmes's works have averaged two yuan per word. Twenty years ago, someone made a statistic of Conan Doyle's writing income, and the total was 400,000 yuan.

Forty years ago, the young Kipling, like the young Conan Doyle, would have been happier to receive one or two hundred yuan for their work than to receive ten or twenty thousand yuan. Moreover, the one or two hundred yuan at that time could help them suffer less material hardship. When Kipling went from London to New York with two proud manuscripts, "Many Inventions" and "The Story of the Gadsbys," he said to the publisher, "There are countless Indian stories in here, countless interesting Indian stories." He almost wanted to hang up a big discount banner like the Shanghai stores, saying, "I'm having a big sale!" Indeed, Kipling was eager to "ship goods" at that time. He only asked for fifty yuan for that manuscript. However, most publishers smiled and shook their heads at him, saying, "We are not interested in Indian stories." Kipling was desperate, but in this despair, a glimmer of new hope arose. An editor heard his bitter pleas and generously offered fifty yuan to buy one of his manuscripts. But when he brought it back and looked at it carefully, he regretted it. "What is this?" the editor said as he stuffed the manuscript into a drawer and left it to rot.

A few years later, Kipling's novel "A Man from Nowhere" was published. At that time, he was at the height of his fame, and sales were booming. The author and editor were gathered together, congratulating each other. When the editor saw Kipling, he suddenly remembered something. He said, "What's going on? Oh, aren't you Mr. Kipling? Oh no, that novel is still in my drawer!" As he said this, he stopped drinking and hurried to the office to find Kipling's novel from a pile of discarded manuscripts. He immediately urged the typesetting room to print it.

The story is getting further and further away, almost from "writers and their remuneration" to anecdotes about writers. Let me talk about two more people and bring this to a close. I have already talked about Scott above, but now I have a few more words to add. When his literary fame was at its peak, he received 40,000 yuan for each of his novels. Unfortunately, from 1826 to 1828, Scott's publishing business suffered heavy losses. In these years, his income from manuscripts reached 200,000 yuan, and he used almost all of this 200,000 yuan to pay back his creditors. In 1851, nineteen years after his death, Adam Black paid 27,000 gold pounds to buy the reprinting rights to many of his novels. Two years later, Routledge bought most of his novels for 100,000 yuan and reprinted them on cheap paper so that the selling price would be low enough for the general readers to afford.

The Irish poet Thomas Moore owed 15,000 yuan and was unable to repay it. Byron knew about it and immediately wrote a novel and gave it to him. This was not a mere empty gesture of friendship, because Mr. Loueman paid 15,000 yuan to buy the copyright, and knowing that Moore was poor, he also gave him 8,000 yuan. Byron's emphasis on chivalry and righteousness is also evident.

Manuscript Guidelines for the Art World

(1) Texts are limited to news, reviews, and introductions related to recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature at home and abroad.

Pictures are limited to recent works by new artists at home and abroad and accompanying illustrations related to the text.

(3) Photographs are limited to recent portraits and works by artists at home and abroad and various photographs related to the text.

(4) The number of words in each text should not exceed 3,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, do not write carelessly, and Western texts should be omitted as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw the illustrations attached to the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. White paper and ink must be used for drawing.

(8) Please indicate that the manuscript is for the Art World section.

(9) All incoming manuscripts will not be returned, whether published or not. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for texts is divided into three types: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand words. The same applies to pictures and photographs, per piece. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be determined separately.

Women's Life

Jinan University Female Students Hold March 8th Women's Day Commemoration: Wang Ying

Jinan University female students held a March 8th Women's Day commemoration meeting today, inviting celebrities to give speeches, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now, the article "March 8th and Chinese Women" submitted by Wang Ying, a female student of the school, is published below.

March 8th is the International Women's Day anniversary, and it is also a good opportunity for female intellectuals to unite comrades and seek practical emancipation for women.

International women, because they could not endure the pain of oppression, there was the production of the Copenhagen Congress in Denmark on March 8, 1909. As a result, it was decided that March 8th would be Women's Day. Its purpose is to seek bread and peace, and to protect female workers. In 1910, women from Germany and Austria also gathered more than 20,000 women in Vienna to hold a large-scale demonstration. Later, countries responded, and every "March 8th," women would gather to hold a conference, on the one hand to express commemoration, and on the other hand to put forward the items that women themselves require, compile them into slogans, so as to arouse the attention of women and men from all walks of life in the society, and to implement the policy of emancipation.

The reason why international women can have their current status—escaping the pain of oppression, the equality of economic status between women and men, and the equality of professional status between women and men—is all related to the effect of the women's movement. Look at the women in our China. Even now, they still cannot completely escape the pain of oppression. The economic status of women and men still cannot be fully equal. The professional status of women and men also has many inequalities. In recent years, although there have been a few lucky ones who have had the opportunity to receive education, there are still a very large number of pitiful insects who are swallowing their voices and enduring, suffering from the heavy oppression in the society, living that inhuman life, and not daring to struggle and resist a little bit, as if waiting there, the female savior and the enlightened in the intellectual world, to find ways to rescue them from the fiery pit for the pitiful insects.

Chinese women have many sufferings, which cannot be described in detail for a while, and are limited by the length of the article. Only the most painful ones are briefly described as follows: (1) The suffering of prostitutes. The life of prostitutes is the most bitter. They must force a smile when they are not happy, force themselves to drink when they cannot win, force themselves to accompany when they are not happy, and force themselves to sing when they are not feeling well. If they encounter guests with bad tempers, they will be insulted and scolded if they do not agree with them, otherwise they will be trampled all night, which is unbearable. Alas, their lives are really not as good as pigs and dogs. Look at the wild chickens soliciting customers by the roadside in Shanghai every night. Their pitiful state is really better than beggars. (2) The suffering of peasant and worker women. They work like cattle and horses all day long, and the rewards they get are extremely small. If they encounter family members with bad tempers, they will be beaten and scolded even more, giving them inhuman treatment. (3) The suffering of women in old etiquette families. The slave life of male supremacy and female inferiority, marriage is not autonomous, and women will never have the opportunity to study.

In short, the suffering of Chinese women is difficult to describe in a word. The current March 8th is the only life-saving festival for our Chinese women. Therefore, we must expand publicity, gather women from all walks of life, and invite male comrades from all walks of life who are enthusiastic about the women's movement to hold a commemorative meeting, and jointly discuss the vital issues and demands of women. We must work hard and strive to attack towards the bright road, and we will not stop until we reach our goal. Our slogans are: 1. Protect oppressed women who escape marriage. 2. Speed up the establishment of agricultural and industrial women's schools. 3. Speed up the establishment of children's foster homes. 4. Abolish prostitution. 5. Speed up the establishment of women's crafts so that they can seek economic independence. 6. Formulate women's labor laws based on the principle of equal pay for equal work and protection of motherhood. 7. Oppose child brides. 8. Oppose the keeping of maids. 9. Protect child labor. 10. Break the etiquette of the slave nature of women.

The Malay Dancer by Shi Duo

Although we cannot see spacious and splendid dance halls in Malay folk life, we can hear delicate and sweet singing from deep within the green shade. This singing is the heartfelt melody that comes from the mouths of Malay dancers. Some of them make dancing and singing their livelihood, while others treat it as a part-time job, only coming out when they have free time from farming. These dancers are sometimes middle-aged women, sometimes girls of sixteen. Except for a few young girls, most of them are married women. Generally, in a dance troupe, besides one or two dancers, there are also several drummers and one or two clowns, a group of seven or eight people, singing everywhere. When business becomes slow in this city, they move to another city. Their whereabouts are uncertain.

In the evening, they come out in full dress and begin to dance and sing. Under the green trees, they set up a grass shed with four wooden poles, and spread straw mats on the ground. They dance on the straw mats, singing and interspersing with the strange noises of the clowns. Sometimes gentle, sometimes strong, it really makes people burst into laughter. When a customer wants to patronize them, they throw a handkerchief or other light object into the performance area. Soon, the clown leads the dancer to the customer. The dancer's feet originally have copper bells, so when she walks, they make a "jing zha jing zha" sound. Naturally, a crowd of viewers, big and small, follows this sound.

When the dancer reaches the customer, she naturally has a set of social etiquette. Then, she clears her throat and sings a captivating clear song. After singing, the customer gives payment, and with a smile, she returns to the performance area, waiting for the second customer to patronize her. Going back and forth like this, they finish their performance and return home to rest at midnight, preparing for the next day's work. Such a life is so leisurely and peaceful.

Her Anti-Smoking Edict by Ke

The wind is gentle and the sun is warm, and everything on the earth is filled with the spirit of spring. The withered poplars and grasses in the schoolyard are also sprouting and growing, full of a thriving attitude. The school gate is even more lively and interesting. Rickshaws, carriages, and cars are constantly coming and going, a veritable stream of carriages and horses, a beautiful sight to behold. He or she, each carrying boxes, bedding, baskets, and briefcases, their faces filled with smiles. Greetings and handshakes all express their intense happiness at reuniting after a brief separation. She, who had not returned home for the winter vacation and had long been lonely, finally looked forward to the start of school. Seeing this lively scene, she couldn't help but run around and wander about. In the classrooms, in the corridors, or in a house that was not often noticed or visited, she could see him and her, whispering sweet nothings to each other, even more intimate than usual. She held a cold and stern

Page 30

attitude, and went to places where the price was high.

"Mo, where are you going alone? Our good friends Miss Zhou and Miss Yi have come. Let's go see them," Qian said, taking her hand and walking away. Turning a corner in the corridor, they heard the laughter of Miss Zhou, Miss Yi, and several other classmates coming from a lounge. She and Qian walked in, and everyone greeted them with smiles. There were five people sitting in the room: Zhou and Yi, Zhou's lover Mr. Cheng, Yi's lover Mr. Wang, and a male classmate named Chen.

"Qian, do you have cigarettes? Wang is craving them badly. Do a good deed and give him one to smoke," Cheng said, smiling at Yi.

"I don't smoke. Ask someone else," Qian hadn't finished speaking when Chen interrupted, "I have them, I have them!" He rummaged in his pocket and took out a cigarette case, handed it to Wang, who took one out, but Chen didn't smoke it himself, instead offering it to Cheng, saying, "I know you secretly smoked a cigarette this morning. Now your addiction is acting up again, but you don't dare say it, so you're using me as an excuse. I get dizzy just smelling cigarette smoke!" Cheng took the cigarette, threw it on the ground, stomped on it, and said with a laugh, "You little rascal, you're really good at talking! Wait till I take care of you!" He ran over and pressed Wang's head down until they were almost kissing, and Wang laughed so hard he couldn't breathe, stammering, "Please spare me! Miss Yi, please say something!" She

saw them making such a fuss over a cigarette, and couldn't help but

ask Qian in surprise,

"Cheng and Wang usually love to smoke. Why do they seem to hate cigarettes now?"

"Oh, don't you know? Because Yi and Zhou don't like cigarette smoking, they issued a smoking ban, so the two of them don't smoke now. But they each don't want to admit it themselves, so they have to tease and provoke each other to ask for it."

"Ah, according to Qian, any government smoking bans or group anti-smoking campaigns are not as effective as such obedience to orders! If every 'he' and 'she' in all of China were like Yi and Zhou, and issued a smoking ban to 'her,' then the future of smoking cessation in China would be very optimistic, and we wouldn't need those official platitudes," Chen said with a laugh. Wang and Cheng felt a little embarrassed to be exposed, while Zhou and Yi smiled serenely, expressing the infinite joy in their hearts.

Guidelines for Women's Life Manuscripts

(1) The content should be about discussions of women's issues, news about women in China and abroad, and descriptions of women's lives. Advocacy is the scope, and the style is not limited.

(2) Manuscripts should be related to women's issues.

(3) Photos related to women's news, women's issues, and women's lives are acceptable. Individual submissions are welcome.

(4) The number of words in a manuscript should not exceed two thousand.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not write in a sloppy manner. Western text should be abbreviated as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink or use colored paper. White paper and black ink must be used.

(8) Please indicate that submissions should be sent to the Women's Life Department.

(9) Whether a manuscript is published or not, it will not be returned. If a return is required, it must be stated in advance and sufficient postage must be attached.

(10) Remuneration for manuscripts is three yuan, two yuan, or one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to drawings and photographs. Remuneration for special manuscripts will be calculated separately.
